data-file-height="198" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Enda Kenny</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">(\xc3\x89anna \xc3\x93 Coinnigh)</i> born 24 April 1951) is an Irish former <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a> politician who served as <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> from 2011 to 2017, <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_Fine_Gael" title="Leader of Fine Gael">Leader of Fine Gael</a> from 2002 to 2017, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Defence_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Defence (Ireland)">Minister for Defence</a> from May 2014 to July 2014 and 2016 to 2017, <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Ireland)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Ireland)">Leader of the Opposition</a> from 2002 to 2011, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Tourism,_Culture,_Arts,_Gaeltacht,_Sport_and_Media" title="Minister for Tourism, Culture, Arts, Gaeltacht, Sport and Media">Minister for Tourism and Trade</a> from 1994 to 1997 and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_at_the_Department_of_Labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of State at the Department of Labour">Minister of State at the Department of Labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_at_the_Department_of_Education" title="Minister of State at the Department of Education">at the Department of Education</a> with responsibility for Youth Affairs from 1986 to 1987. He served as <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">Teachta D\xc3\xa1la</a> (TD) for <a href="/wiki/Mayo_West_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Mayo West (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Mayo West</a> from 1975 to 1997 and for <a href="/wiki/Mayo_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Mayo (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Mayo</a> from 1997 to 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas_db_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas_db-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny led <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a> to a historic victory at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_general_election" title="2011 Irish general election">2011 general election</a>, his party becoming the largest in the state for the first time, forming a coalition government with the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a> on 9 March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Coalition_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coalition-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He subsequently became the first Fine Gael member to be elected Taoiseach for a second consecutive term on 6 May 2016, after <a href="/wiki/2016_Irish_government_formation" title="2016 Irish government formation">two months of negotiations</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/2016_Irish_general_election" title="2016 Irish general election">2016 election</a>, forming a Fine Gael-led <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reelection_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reelection-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He was the first Taoiseach from Fine Gael since <a href="/wiki/John_Bruton" title="John Bruton">John Bruton</a> (1994\xe2\x80\x931997), and the first Leader of Fine Gael to win a general election since <a href="/wiki/Garret_FitzGerald" title="Garret FitzGerald">Garret FitzGerald</a> in 1982. He became the longest-serving Fine Gael Taoiseach in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-RTE-LongestFG01a_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTE-LongestFG01a-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny stepped down as Leader of Fine Gael on 2 June 2017, and announced he would resign as Taoiseach once a new leader was chosen in early June.<sup id="cite_ref-Resignation_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resignation-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In the following <a href="/wiki/2017_Fine_Gael_leadership_election" title="2017 Fine Gael leadership election">leadership election</a>, the then <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Social_Protection" title="Minister for Social Protection">Minister for Social Protection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a>, was elected to succeed him as Leader of Fine Gael.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Kenny tendered his resignation as Taoiseach on 13 June 2017, and was succeeded by Varadkar the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-Farewell_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farewell-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> On 5 November 2017, Kenny announced that he would not contest the <a href="/wiki/2020_Irish_general_election" title="2020 Irish general election">following general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a (1975\xe2\x80\x931994)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Minister_for_Tourism_(1994\xe2\x80\x931997)"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Minister for class="tocnumber">2.7.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ministerial pay cuts</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-16"><a href="#Financial_and_banking_policy"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Financial and banking policy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-17"><a href="#Pension_levy_controversy"><span <span class="toctext">2013</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-22"><a href="#Promissory_notes"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Promissory notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-23"><a href="#Magdalene_Laundry_apology"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Magdalene Laundry apology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-24"><a href="#Second_national_address"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Second national address</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25"><a href="#2014"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.3</span> <span class="toctext">2014</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-26"><a href="#Resignations_of_Martin_Callinan_and_Alan_Shatter"><span class="tocnumber">2.7.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Resignations of Martin Callinan and Alan Shatter</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#2015"><span class="tocnumber">2.8</span> <span class="toctext">2015</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#2016"><span class="tocnumber">2.9</span> <span class="toctext">2016</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#2017"><span class="tocnumber">2.10</span> <span class="toctext">2017</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Retirement"><span class="tocnumber">2.11</span> <span class="toctext">Retirement</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Post-political_activity"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Post-political activity</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Return_to_the_backbenches_(2017\xe2\x80\x932020)"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Return to the backbenches (2017\xe2\x80\x932020)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Legacy"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Kenny was born in 1951 in Derrycoosh, <a href="/wiki/Islandeady" title="Islandeady">Islandeady</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Castlebar" title="Castlebar">Castlebar</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Mayo" title="County Mayo">County Mayo</a>, the third child of five of Mary Eithne (McGinley) and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kenny" title="Henry Kenny">Henry Kenny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He was educated locally at St Patrick\'s National School, Cornanool N.S, <a href="/wiki/Leitir_N.S" class="mw-redirect" title="Leitir N.S">Leitir N.S</a> and at <a href="/wiki/St_Gerald%27s_College,_Castlebar" title="St Gerald&#39;s College, Castlebar">St. Gerald\'s College</a>, Castlebar.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He attended <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_College,_Dublin" title="St Patrick&#39;s College, Dublin">St Patrick\'s College, Dublin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whoisendakenny_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoisendakenny-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> qualifying as a national teacher and was an undergraduate student at <a href="/wiki/NUI_Galway" title="NUI Galway">University College Galway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He worked as a primary school teacher for four years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He also played football for his local club <a href="/wiki/Islandeady_GAA" title="Islandeady GAA">Islandeady GAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Early_years_in_D.C3.A1il_.C3.89ireann_.281975.E2.80.931994.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_in_D\xc3\xa1il_\xc3\x89ireann_(1975\xe2\x80\x931994)">Early years in D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann (1975\xe2\x80\x931994)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years in D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann (1975\xe2\x80\x931994)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Kenny was exposed to politics from an early age, following his father Henry Kenny, becoming a Fine Gael TD in <a href="/wiki/1954_Irish_general_election" title="1954 Irish general election">1954</a>. In the early 1970s, he became directly involved in politics when he started helping his father with constituency clinics. In 1975, Henry Kenny (who was at this stage a <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_(Ireland)" title="Minister of State (Ireland)">Parliamentary Secretary</a> in the government) died after a short battle with cancer. Fine Gael wanted one of his sons to stand as their candidate at the <a href="/wiki/1975_Mayo_West_by-election" class="mw-redirect" title="1975 Mayo West by-election">subsequent by-election</a>, and so Enda Kenny was chosen. He was elected on the first count with 52% of the vote, and thus became the youngest member of the <a href="/wiki/20th_D%C3%A1il" class="mw-redirect" title="20th D\xc3\xa1il">20th D\xc3\xa1il</a>, aged 24.<sup id="cite_ref-elecs_irl_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elecs_irl-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny remained on the backbenches for almost a decade. He was appointed party spokesperson firstly on Youth Affairs and Sport,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> then Western Development; however, he failed to build a national profile as he concentrated more on constituency matters. Kenny was left out in the cold when <a href="/wiki/Garret_FitzGerald" title="Garret FitzGerald">Garret FitzGerald</a> became <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> for the first time in 1981, and again in 1982. He was, however, appointed as a member of the Fine Gael delegation at the <a href="/wiki/New_Ireland_Forum" title="New Ireland Forum">New Ireland Forum</a> in 1983. He later served on the British-Irish Parliamentary Association. In 1986, he became a <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_at_the_Department_of_Labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of State at the Department of Labour">Minister of State at the Department of Labour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_at_the_Department_of_Education" title="Minister of State at the Department of Education">at the Department of Education</a> with responsibility for Youth Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Fine Gael lost the <a href="/wiki/1987_Irish_general_election" title="1987 Irish general election">1987 general election</a>, resulting in Kenny and Fine Gael being on the opposition benches for the next seven years. In spite of this, his national profile was raised as he served in a number of positions on the party\'s <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael_Front_Bench" title="Fine Gael Front Bench">front bench</a>, including Education, Arts, Heritage, <a href="/wiki/Gaeltacht" title="Gaeltacht">Gaeltacht</a>, and the Islands. He was also the Fine Gael <a href="/wiki/Chief_Whip" title="Chief Whip">Chief Whip</a> for a short period.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Minister_for_Tourism_.281994.E2.80.931997.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Minister_for_Tourism_(1994\xe2\x80\x931997)">Minister for Tourism (1994\xe2\x80\x931997)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Minister for Tourism (1994\xe2\x80\x931997)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In late 1994, the <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna F\xc3\xa1il">Fianna F\xc3\xa1il</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a> government collapsed; however, no general election was called. Instead, a <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a>\xe2\x80\x93Labour Party\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_(Ireland)" title="Democratic Left (Ireland)">Democratic Left</a> "<a href="/wiki/24th_Government_of_Ireland" title="24th Government of Ireland">Rainbow Coalition</a>" came to power. Kenny, as Fine Gael chief whip, was a key member of the team, which negotiated the programme for government with the other parties prior to the formation of the new government. Under Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/John_Bruton" title="John Bruton">John Bruton</a>, Kenny joined the cabinet and was appointed <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Tourism,_Culture,_Arts,_Gaeltacht,_Sport_and_Media" title="Minister for Tourism, Culture, Arts, Gaeltacht, Sport and Media">Minister for Tourism and Trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> During his tenure as Minister, Ireland saw a significant growth in the tourism sector and in its international trade position.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As Minister, he chaired the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> Council of Trade Ministers, during Ireland\'s six-month <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">Presidency of the European Council</a>, as well as co-chairing a round of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> talks in 1996. Among Kenny\'s other achievements were the rejuvenation of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Day" title="Saint Patrick&#39;s Day">Saint Patrick\'s Day</a> parade in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the successful negotiations to bring a stage of the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> to Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, the government was defeated at the <a href="/wiki/1997_Irish_general_election" title="1997 Irish general election">general election</a> and Kenny returned to the opposition benches.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Opposition_.281997.E2.80.932011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_(1997\xe2\x80\x932011)">Opposition (1997\xe2\x80\x932011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Opposition (1997\xe2\x80\x932011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_Gael_leadership_elections">Fine Gael leadership elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Fine Gael leadership elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2001">2001</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2001">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p><a href="/wiki/John_Bruton" title="John Bruton">John Bruton</a> resigned as leader of Fine Gael in 2001, following a vote of no confidence in his ability.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Kenny stood in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Fine_Gael_leadership_election" title="2001 Fine Gael leadership election">subsequent leadership election</a>, promising to "electrify the party".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In the final ballot it was <a href="/wiki/Michael_Noonan_(Fine_Gael_politician)" title="Michael Noonan (Fine Gael politician)">Michael Noonan</a> who emerged victorious (it is Fine Gael\'s custom not to publish ballot results for leadership elections). Noonan did not give a spokesperson\'s assignment to Kenny; this led him to accuse Noonan of sending a "dangerous message".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="2002">2002</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2002">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2002_Irish_general_election" title="2002 Irish general election">2002 general election</a>, Fine Gael suffered its worst electoral performance ever, losing 23 seats, a figure larger than expected, with its share of the vote down 5%. Kenny himself came close to losing his seat, and even went so far as to prepare a concession speech. In the end he <a href="/wiki/Mayo_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)#2002_general_election" title="Mayo (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">won the third seat in the five-seat constituency</a>. Noonan resigned as Fine Gael leader on the night of the result, an action which triggered another <a href="/wiki/2002_Fine_Gael_leadership_election" title="2002 Fine Gael leadership election">leadership election</a>. Protest meetings were held by members of the party against the speed with which the leadership election had been called and the failure to broaden the franchise to the membership. It was suggested<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2016)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that it was foolish to choose a leader before conducting an electoral post-mortem.\n</p><p>Kenny once again contested the leadership and emerged successful on that occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-rte_fg_leader_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte_fg_leader-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_(7).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_%287%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_%287%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_%287%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_%287%29.jpg 1.5x, 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_LEADERS_MEET_IN_DUBLIN_14_April_2008_(7).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Enda Kenny shakes the hand of <a href="/wiki/German_Chancellor" class="mw-redirect" title="German Chancellor">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> in April 2008</div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="Racist_remarks_.282002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Racist_remarks_(2002)">Racist remarks (2002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Racist remarks (2002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2002, Kenny was accused of making racist remarks after he used the word "nigger" in a joke relating to <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, the assassinated first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo">Prime Minister of the Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>. Kenny wanted the incident to be suppressed, and specifically asked journalists not to cite it, though the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Independent_(Ireland)" title="Sunday Independent (Ireland)">Sunday Independent</a></i> newspaper reported his "chortling repetition of the inflammatory word".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> He was subsequently condemned by race campaigners at home and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Matters were made worse when it emerged that several of Lumumba\'s relatives, including a son and several grandchildren, lived in <a href="/wiki/Tallaght" title="Tallaght">Tallaght</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny apologized unreservedly but insisted that there was no racist intent, and that he was merely quoting what a Moroccan barman had once said, while reminiscing about an incident he had witnessed in the company of his friend <a href="/wiki/David_Molony" title="David Molony">David Molony</a>, whose sudden death had recently occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes2002-09-09-01a_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes2002-09-09-01a-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> However, what he said was widely seen as politically indefensible, as a story that should not have been told in the company of reporters by someone hoping to become the next Taoiseach.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishTimes2002-09-09-01a_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishTimes2002-09-09-01a-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Leader_of_the_Opposition_.282002.E2.80.932011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Leader_of_the_Opposition_(2002\xe2\x80\x932011)">Leader of the Opposition (2002\xe2\x80\x932011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Leader of the Opposition (2002\xe2\x80\x932011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fine Gael out-performed expectations at the 2004 <a href="/wiki/2004_Irish_local_elections" title="2004 Irish local elections">Local</a> and <a href="/wiki/2004_European_Parliament_election_in_Ireland" title="2004 European Parliament election in Ireland">European</a> elections, which saw Fine Gael increase its representation from 4 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a> of 15 from Ireland, to 5 from 13. This was the first time Fine Gael had ever defeated Fianna F\xc3\xa1il in a national election, as well as the first time Fianna F\xc3\xa1il had failed to finish first in a national election since its second place in the <a href="/wiki/September_1927_Irish_general_election" title="September 1927 Irish general election">1927 general election</a> behind <a href="/wiki/Cumann_na_nGaedheal" title="Cumann na nGaedheal">Cumann na nGaedheal</a>, Fine Gael\'s immediate predecessor.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_(39).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_%2839%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_europeanpeoplesparty_-_EPP_Summit_11_December_2008_(39).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Hungary" title="Prime Minister of Hungary">Prime Minister of Hungary</a> <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orb\xc3\xa1n">Viktor Orb\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacek_Saryusz-Wolski" title="Jacek Saryusz-Wolski">Jacek Saryusz-Wolski</a>, and Enda Kenny during an <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">EPP</a> Summit in December 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>In July 2005, <a href="/wiki/Rossport_Five" title="Rossport Five">five men</a> from the north of Kenny\'s Mayo constituency were jailed over their opposition to the Fianna F\xc3\xa1il-led government\'s plans for the <a href="/wiki/Corrib_gas_project" title="Corrib gas project">Corrib gas project</a>. One of the men, Philip McGrath, worked for Kenny as an election agent for <a href="/wiki/Rossport" title="Rossport">Rossport</a> during general elections. Unlike his fellow Mayo Fine Gael TD, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ring" title="Michael Ring">Michael Ring</a>, Kenny was cautious about backing the men\'s stance (Ring would later be forced to adopt the same policy).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shell_to_Sea" title="Shell to Sea">Shell to Sea</a> campaign that was founded to help release the men and get the government to change its mind shut down work on the project for fifteen months. When <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda\xc3\xad</a> were brought in to remove protesters with tactics that saw many hospitalised, Kenny said: "The law must be obeyed."<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2005, Kenny called for the abolition of compulsory Irish for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Leaving_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Leaving Certificate">Leaving Certificate</a> examinations. This was opposed by all the major <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> In March 2006, he was elected Vice-President of the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a> (EPP), the largest European political group to which Fine Gael is affiliated.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In his speech to the EPP, he stated that Fine Gael would be in government in Ireland within two years.\n</p><p>During the first half of 2006, Kenny went aggressively after a more populist line on the cost of immigration, street crime, <a href="/wiki/Paedophilia" class="mw-redirect" title="Paedophilia">paedophilia</a> and homeowners\' rights. A graphic description of a mugging he had experienced was given to the D\xc3\xa1il, in the context of a crime discussion, only for it to be revealed a day later that the incident had occurred in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, not in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg/170px-EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg/255px-EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg/340px-EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EndaKenny2007FineGael.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenny, speaking at the <a href="/wiki/Young_Fine_Gael" title="Young Fine Gael">Young Fine Gael</a> conference in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Under Kenny, Fine Gael agreed to enter a pre-election pact with the Labour Party, to offer the electorate an alternative coalition government at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Irish_general_election" title="2007 Irish general election">2007 general election</a> held on 24 May 2007. The so-called Mullingar Accord was agreed in September 2004, following the European and local elections that year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(Ireland)" title="Green Party (Ireland)">Green Party</a> also signalled via the media to be in favour of membership of such a coalition government after the election.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> However, it would not commit to an agreement before polling day.\n</p><p>Kenny\'s leadership attempted to define Fine Gael as a party of the progressive centre. Its policy initiatives concentrated on value for money, consumer rights, civil partnerships, reform of public spending, reward and enterprise and preventative health care policy. The party sought to retake its former mantle as the law-and-order and a party committed to defending the institutions of the state. At the Fine Gael <a href="/wiki/Ardfheis" title="Ardfheis">Ardfheis</a> in March 2007, Kenny outlined his platform for the forthcoming general election entitled the "Contract for a Better Ireland".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The main aspects of this "contract" included: 2,300 more hospital beds, 2,000 more <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda\xc3\xad</a>, tougher jail sentences and tougher bail for criminals, free health insurance for all children under 16 and lower income tax.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Bertie Ahern was perceived by many to have comfortably beaten Kenny in the pre-election Leaders\' debate.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> When the votes were counted it emerged that Fine Gael had made large gains, increasing its number of seats by twenty, to give a total of 51 seats in the new D\xc3\xa1il.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> However, Labour and the Greens failed to make gains, leaving Kenny\'s "Alliance for Change" short of a majority. Despite predictions to the contrary, the Fianna F\xc3\xa1il vote recovered sufficiently to bring it to 78 seats, and a third term in government for Ahern.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Responding to the <a href="/wiki/Post-2008_Irish_banking_crisis" title="Post-2008 Irish banking crisis">banking crisis</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Cork" title="County Cork">County Cork</a>, on 15 February 2009, Kenny asked the entire board of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Ireland" title="Central Bank of Ireland">Central Bank of Ireland</a>\'s Financial Regulation section to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenny_wants_Regulator_board_to_resign_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenny_wants_Regulator_board_to_resign-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_challenge_to_leadership">2010 challenge to leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2010 challenge to leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>An opinion poll published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Irish_Times" title="The Irish Times">The Irish Times</a></i> on 10 June 2010 triggered a challenge to Kenny\'s leadership of the party. The Ipsos MRBI poll indicated that the Labour Party had become the most popular political party in the country for the first time, and also showed a drop in backing for Fianna F\xc3\xa1il and Fine Gael, and for their leaders. It showed a five-point drop in Fianna F\xc3\xa1il support since January 2010, leaving that party on 17%, Fine Gael down four points to 28%, and Labour up eight points to 32%. Satisfaction with Kenny\'s leadership dropped 7% to 24%.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_15062010-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the failure of the party\'s deputy leader <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruton" title="Richard Bruton">Richard Bruton</a> to support him, he was dismissed by Kenny on 14 June 2010. He also tabled a motion of confidence in his leadership, to be held on 17 June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_15062010-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_14062010_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_14062010-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On the following day it was revealed that nine members of the Fine Gael frontbench did not have confidence in Kenny to lead their party \xe2\x80\x93 composed of <a href="/wiki/Simon_Coveney" title="Simon Coveney">Simon Coveney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denis_Naughten" title="Denis Naughten">Denis Naughten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olwyn_Enright" title="Olwyn Enright">Olwyn Enright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Mitchell" title="Olivia Mitchell">Olivia Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fergus_O%27Dowd" title="Fergus O&#39;Dowd">Fergus O\'Dowd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Creed" title="Michael Creed">Michael Creed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Timmins" title="Billy Timmins">Billy Timmins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Hayes_(politician)" title="Brian Hayes (politician)">Brian Hayes</a>. Denis Naughten said frontbench members did not have Kenny\'s support and would like him to withdraw his motion of confidence and stand down in the interest of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_No_Conf_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_No_Conf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2008, <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Browne" title="Vincent Browne">Vincent Browne</a> criticised Kenny in <i>The Irish Times</i> for not having a grasp of the issues, notably of economic issues.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The motion of confidence in Kenny was passed.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_No_Conf_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_15062010_No_Conf-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_17062010_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_17062010-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He announced a major reshuffle of his party\'s front bench on 1 July 2010, re-appointing Bruton, Coveney, O\'Dowd, and Varadkar.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_general_election">2011 general election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2011 general election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the start of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_general_election" title="2011 Irish general election">2011 general election</a> campaign, Kenny said Fine Gael recognised the importance of "the giving of hope and confidence to people through the taxation system", when speaking to reporters outside party election headquarters in Dublin. "The Fine Gael party in this election is the only party that is categorically saying that there will not be any increase in income tax over our period in government", he said. He said the country needed strong government and not an administration that depended on the support of Independents. "I think that this is a time for courageous and strong government. It is not a time for government that might self-combust or that would be dependent on the whim of any mercenary Independents. This is a judgment call for the people."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was several leaders debates on television during the campaign. There were, uniquely, three debates on stations <a href="/wiki/TV3_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="TV3 Ireland">TV3</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89">RT\xc3\x89</a> and <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a>, between Enda Kenny, Micha\xc3\xa9l Martin and Eamon Gilmore, and a five-way leaders\' debate on RT\xc3\x89 which also included <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams" title="Gerry Adams">Gerry Adams</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Gormley" title="John Gormley">John Gormley</a>, along with the other participants from the three-way debates.\n</p><p>Kenny, however, refused to participate in the three-way leaders\' debate proposed by <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="TV3 (Ireland)">TV3</a>, stating his unhappiness that <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Browne" title="Vincent Browne">Vincent Browne</a> was to chair the debate.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Browne is a well-known critic of Fine Gael and Kenny. In 1982, Browne appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_(Irish_talk_show)" title="The Late Late Show (Irish talk show)">The Late Late Show</a></i> where he poured scorn on Kenny, claiming he was "purporting" to be a TD.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In October 2010, Browne was forced to make a public apology to Kenny after jokingly asking whether Fine Gael was requesting that he go into a <a href="/wiki/Darkroom" title="Darkroom">darkroom</a> with a gun and a bottle of whisky. This was in reference to Fine Gael\'s position in the polls, where they were in second place to Labour, and a previous leadership challenge to Kenny by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruton" title="Richard Bruton">Richard Bruton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Kenny refused to appear on the leaders debate despite an offer by Browne to be replaced by a different moderator for the debate if Kenny would appear.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny participated in a three-party leader debate on RT\xc3\x89 moderated by <a href="/wiki/Miriam_O%27Callaghan" title="Miriam O&#39;Callaghan">Miriam O\'Callaghan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and also in a five-way debate on RT\xc3\x89; this was a new format, involving all party leaders of the outgoing D\xc3\xa1il, including Kenny, moderated by <a href="/wiki/Pat_Kenny" title="Pat Kenny">Pat Kenny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He participated in a three-way debate in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> with Miche\xc3\xa1l Martin and Eamon Gilmore on TG4.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 February 2011, Kenny met <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic_of_Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic of Germany)">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> to discuss the Irish economy. Kenny and Merkel have close political ties because Merkel\'s <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">CDU party</a> and Fine Gael are both members of the centre-right <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a> (EPP), and seating at EPP meetings is arranged by <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a> of surname.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The close relationship between these two leaders is illustrated further by the fact that Angela Merkel also backed Enda Kenny and Fine Gael during the 2007 election.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg/220px-Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg/330px-Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg/440px-Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3543" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enda_Kenny%27s_2011_General_Election_Victory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenny makes a speech to Fine Gael party members on the day of the election results</div></div></div>\n<p>Opinion polls of 23 February 2011, sponsored by <i><a href="/wiki/Paddy_Power" title="Paddy Power">Paddy Power</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Independent" title="Irish Independent">Irish Independent</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and <i>The Irish Times</i><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> suggested that Kenny would lead Fine Gael to its largest total of seats to date in the <a href="/wiki/31st_D%C3%A1il" class="mw-redirect" title="31st D\xc3\xa1il">31st D\xc3\xa1il</a>, and that he would be elected Taoiseach.\n</p><p>In the election, Kenny led Fine Gael to a decisive victory. The party won 76 seats, the most in its 78-year history, becoming the largest party in the D\xc3\xa1il for the first time. Meanwhile, Fianna F\xc3\xa1il suffered the worst defeat of a sitting government in the history of the Irish state, its representation being reduced by 75%. Kenny himself topped the poll in his Mayo constituency and uniquely three others from Fine Gael were elected alongside Kenny. At a victory party in Dublin, Kenny declared Fine Gael had "a massive endorsement" to govern, and the election marked "a transformative moment in Ireland\'s history".<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Later, he told <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann">RT\xc3\x89</a> that he fully expected to become Taoiseach after what he called "a democratic revolution at the ballot box".<sup id="cite_ref-Revolution_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revolution-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> While there was some talk that Fine Gael would govern alone as a minority government, senior Fine Gael leaders indicated as soon as the election result was beyond doubt that they would likely enter a coalition government with the Labour Party.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Late on the night of 5 March 2011, at <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Castle" title="Dublin Castle">Dublin Castle</a>, Fine Gael and Labour formally agreed to form a coalition government with Kenny as Taoiseach<sup id="cite_ref-Coalition_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coalition-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and Labour leader <a href="/wiki/Eamon_Gilmore" title="Eamon Gilmore">Eamon Gilmore</a> as <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a>, with Labour being given four other seats in cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-Tanaiste_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanaiste-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny said that his first priority upon taking office would be to renegotiate the terms of the bailout for Ireland, calling the original deal "a bad deal for Ireland and a bad deal for Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="13th_Taoiseach_.282011.E2.80.932017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="13th_Taoiseach_(2011\xe2\x80\x932017)">13th Taoiseach (2011\xe2\x80\x932017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 13th Taoiseach (2011\xe2\x80\x932017)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3974" data-file-height="2588" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_and_Enda_Kenny_at_Farmleigh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenny with <a href="/wiki/US_President" class="mw-redirect" title="US President">US President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, 23 May 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_31st_D%C3%A1il" title="Members of the 31st D\xc3\xa1il">members of the 31st D\xc3\xa1il</a> convened for the first time on 9 March 2011, the D\xc3\xa1il elected Kenny as Taoiseach by a vote of 117\xe2\x80\x9327.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Kenny received his seal of office from <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mary_McAleese" title="Mary McAleese">Mary McAleese</a>. He also announced ministerial appointees to his Government on 9 March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> At just under 59 years and 11 months on accession, Kenny is the second-oldest person to have assumed the office for the first time,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> the oldest being <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Lemass" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Lemass">Se\xc3\xa1n Lemass</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 9 March 2011, Kenny appointed 15 junior Ministers. He also appointed a Minister for political reform, and sent a request to the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Public_Works" title="Office of Public Works">Office of Public Works</a> as to how he could address ministerial transport.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On 15 March 2011, it was announced that only the current President, the Taoiseach, the T\xc3\xa1naiste and the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Justice_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Justice (Ireland)">Minister for Justice and Equality</a> were to have Garda drivers. All other Ministers would have to make use of their own transport with a mileage allowance and a commercial chauffeur as an expense. There was no announcement as to the continuing engagement of three government jets.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The media reported that this would reduce the ministerial motor vehicle transport bill to \xe2\x82\xac7,000,000 annually, which is more than the combined annual tax contributions of 16,000 people on <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ministerial_pay_cuts">Ministerial pay cuts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ministerial pay cuts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>In one of his first acts as Taoiseach, Kenny slashed his own pay by \xe2\x82\xac14,000 (a reduction of 7%). The new government also decided to cut the pay of senior Ministers. The Taoiseach\'s pay was cut from \xe2\x82\xac214,187 to \xe2\x82\xac200,000. T\xc3\xa1naiste Eamon Gilmore\'s pay was cut from \xe2\x82\xac197,486 to \xe2\x82\xac184,405. Ministers\' pay was reduced to \xe2\x82\xac169,275 (from \xe2\x82\xac181,283), while pay for Ministers of State was cut from \xe2\x82\xac139,266 to \xe2\x82\xac130,042. In another cost-cutting measure, Kenny asked the Gardai, the Departments of Justice and Transport, as well as the Office of Public Works, to come up with a plan to reduce the amount spent on transporting Ministers and their teams.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_banking_policy">Financial and banking policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Financial and banking policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On 11 March 2011, his third day in office, Kenny attended his first <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> as Taoiseach, in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>. During that summit he engaged in a heated confrontation with <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> (which Kenny termed "a Gallic spat") over Ireland\'s comparatively low 12.5% corporate tax rate, which EU leaders have frequently posited as a condition of more favourable terms for the Irish bailout.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Kenny held firm on his refusal to alter the corporate tax, which he reiterated in his first Leaders\' Questions the following week\xe2\x80\x94also declaring his government\'s intention to withhold further state funds from Dublin banks until the EU agreed to new terms that forced banks\' senior bondholders to share in the losses.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, less than three weeks later on 31 March 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Ireland" title="Central Bank of Ireland">Central Bank of Ireland</a> published the results of its "stress tests" on Ireland\'s four surviving banks (Allied Irish Banks, Bank of Ireland, EBS, and Irish Life &amp; Permanent) \xe2\x80\x94 indicating that the banks needed to raise an additional \xe2\x82\xac24,000,000,000 to remain solvent.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Despite his earlier promise, the government announced the same day that the state would supply the necessary funds to keep the banks afloat, with Kenny stating that seeking the money from bondholders would be neither "reasonable or logical".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny was heavily criticised for his government\'s action, with the <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Independent" title="Irish Independent">Irish Independent</a></i> noting that "this is the fifth time Irish people have been told over the past couple of years it would be the last payout they would have to endure".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nevertheless, the first national opinion poll since Kenny took office, published on 10 April 2011, showed that public support for Kenny\'s Fine Gael party had increased since the election from 36% to 39%, although a plurality also indicated deep dissatisfaction with his rescue of the banks.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 July 2011, Kenny announced that an agreement had been reached by <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> leaders to reduce Ireland\'s interest rate by 2% and extend the repayment period.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Pension_levy_controversy">Pension levy controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Pension levy controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On 9 May 2011, Kenny\'s government announced a new <a href="/wiki/Job_creation_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Job creation program">job creation program</a>, along with plan to finance it via a 0.6% tax levy on private pension savings.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Public pension funds, however, would remain untouched. The pension levy caused an immediate and intense outcry, leaving Kenny to defend the initiative as "a modest proposal" and refuting charges that the government would next tax personal savings.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> However, the controversy surrounding the levy intensified on 12 May 2011, when Kenny admitted that the holders of Approved Retirement Funds\xe2\x80\x94most of whom were among the highest income earners in Ireland\xe2\x80\x94would not be included in the levy.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_reforms">Political reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Political reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On 3 May 2011, Kenny\'s government approved a set of political reforms that adhered to promises he had made in the general election.<sup id="cite_ref-IT-TDs-fall_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IT-TDs-fall-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mayoadv_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mayoadv-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Among the approved reforms were a binding Constituency Commission scheduled for June 2011, with the specific purpose of reducing the number of TDs by up to 20;<sup id="cite_ref-IT-TDs-fall_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IT-TDs-fall-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> an act to establish a six-month time limit for holding by-elections to the D\xc3\xa1il; a \xe2\x82\xac750,000 spending limit in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_presidential_election" title="2011 Irish presidential election">2011 presidential election</a>; legislation to ban corporate donations, to be enacted by summer 2011; establishment of a Constitutional Convention in 2011, which was to include discussion of the Seanad; and a referendum on the abolition of the Seanad, to be held in the second half of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-mayoadv_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mayoadv-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The promise to cut up to 20 TDs caused some controversy and scepticism, due to the Constitutional requirement that there be no less than one TD for every 30,000 people, which would necessitate a minimum of 150 TDs\xe2\x80\x94meaning that the current number of 166 TDs could be reduced by 16 at most.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Vatican_reprimand_and_response">Vatican reprimand and response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Vatican reprimand and response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="38" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:\n<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/D%C3%A1il_Motion:_Commission_of_Investigation_Report_in_the_Catholic_Diocese_of_Cloyne" class="extiw" title="wikisource:D\xc3\xa1il Motion: Commission of Investigation Report in the Catholic Diocese of Cloyne">Enda Kenny\'s Cloyne Speech</a></b></div></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>On 13 July 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse_scandal_in_Cloyne_diocese" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual abuse scandal in Cloyne diocese">Cloyne Report</a> was published, detailing the investigation into allegations of child sexual abuse by 19 priests in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Cloyne" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Cloyne">Roman Catholic Diocese of Cloyne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Among the report\'s findings were the revelation that the vast majority of allegations made in the diocese were not reported to the <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda</a>, as required by the Church\'s 1996 guidelines; that the Bishop of the Diocese, <a href="/wiki/John_Magee_(bishop)" title="John Magee (bishop)">John Magee</a>, and others had withheld full co-operation with the Government\'s investigation and had deliberately misrepresented his own response to the allegations; and that the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> itself had both refused to co-operate in the investigation and counselled the Diocese that the 1996 guidelines were not binding.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 July 2011, <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/D%C3%A1il_Motion:_Commission_of_Investigation_Report_in_the_Catholic_Diocese_of_Cloyne" class="extiw" title="s:D\xc3\xa1il Motion: Commission of Investigation Report in the Catholic Diocese of Cloyne">Kenny condemned the Vatican</a><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> for its role in the scandal, stating that the Church\'s role in obstructing the investigation was a serious infringement upon the sovereignty of Ireland and that the scandal revealed "the dysfunction, disconnection and elitism that dominates the culture of the Vatican to this day".<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He added that "the historic relationship between church and state in Ireland could not be the same again".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny\'s attack on the Vatican was unprecedented by a high-level official in Ireland. The speech was widely regarded as extraordinary, with the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> commenting that the attack was "the first time that Ireland\'s Parliament has publicly castigated the Vatican instead of local church leaders during the country\'s 17 years of paedophile-priest scandals".<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> remarked that " the political classes have...lost their fear, namely of the once almighty Roman Catholic church."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 September, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> issued its response to Kenny\'s speech noting that "the accusation that the Holy See attempted "to frustrate an Inquiry in a sovereign, democratic republic as little as three years ago, not three decades ago", which Mr Kenny made no attempt to substantiate, is unfounded. Indeed, when asked, a Government spokesperson clarified that Mr. Kenny was not referring to any specific incident". The response added that "Those Reports [...] contain no evidence to suggest that the Holy See meddled in the internal affairs of the Irish State or, for that matter, was involved in the day-to-day management of Irish dioceses or religious congregations with respect to sexual abuse issues".\n</p><p>On the quoting of then Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Ratzinger</a>, the response notes that the quotation was taken from the <i>Instruction on the Ecclesial Vocation of the Theologian</i>, otherwise known as <i>Donum Veritatis</i> (The Gift of the Truth), published by the Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith on 24 May 1990, and signed by the then Prefect and Secretary of the Congregation. Therefore, it is not a private text of the then Cardinal Ratzinger but an official document of the Congregation.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="First_national_address">First national address</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: First national address">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="38" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:\n<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/A_National_Address_by_an_Taoiseach,_Enda_Kenny" class="extiw" title="wikisource:A National Address by an Taoiseach, Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny\'s address to the nation</a></b></div></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>Kenny gave a <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/A_National_Address_by_an_Taoiseach,_Enda_Kenny" class="extiw" title="s:A National Address by an Taoiseach, Enda Kenny">televised address to the nation</a> on 4 December 2011, ahead of the delivery of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_budget,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish budget, 2012">2012 Irish budget</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> He warned that Budget 2012 "will be tough", and that "it has to be". He also said that it would move Ireland towards a manageable deficit of 3% of GDP by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> This was only the sixth time that a Taoiseach had addressed the nation,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> reflecting the gravity of the Irish economic condition, in what Kenny stressed were "exceptional" circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-retriever_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retriever-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The broadcast was the second-most watched television programme of 2011 in Ireland, attracting an audience of 1.2&#160;million viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg/220px-Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg/330px-Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg/440px-Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Cabinet_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Taoiseach Enda Kenny, with <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_31st_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 31st D\xc3\xa1il">his cabinet</a> in March 2013</div></div></div>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Promissory_notes">Promissory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Promissory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>In February 2013, a deal was reached with the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a>, in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Promissory_note" title="Promissory note">promissory note</a> used to bail out the former <a href="/wiki/Anglo_Irish_Bank" title="Anglo Irish Bank">Anglo Irish Bank</a>. Kenny described it as "a good day for the country and its people".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He told the D\xc3\xa1il that, as a result of the changes, there would be a \xe2\x82\xac20 billion reduction in the borrowing requirement of the <a href="/wiki/National_Treasury_Management_Agency" title="National Treasury Management Agency">National Treasury Management Agency</a> in the years ahead, but also cautioned that the agreement was not a "silver bullet".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Magdalene_Laundry_apology">Magdalene Laundry apology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Magdalene Laundry apology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On 19 February 2013, Kenny apologised in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a>, on behalf of the State to the <a href="/wiki/Magdalene_asylum" title="Magdalene asylum">survivors of the Magdalene Laundries</a>. The government also told the estimated 800 to 1,000 surviving Magdalene women that a compensation scheme would be set up for them.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> However, by February 2014, none of the 684 applicants had received their statutory old-age pensions or health care benefits promised.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_national_address">Second national address</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Second national address">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>To mark the end of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurozone crisis">Troika bailout</a> in December 2013, Kenny gave a second address to the nation, saying that the country was moving in the right direction, and that the economy was starting to recover.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Finished_09_(14463023943).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg/220px-Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg/330px-Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg/440px-Finished_09_%2814463023943%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Finished_09_(14463023943).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenny meeting members of Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Defence_Forces_(Ireland)" title="Defence Forces (Ireland)">Defence Forces</a> deployed on a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> mission in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a></div></div></div>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Resignations_of_Martin_Callinan_and_Alan_Shatter">Resignations of Martin Callinan and Alan Shatter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Resignations of Martin Callinan and Alan Shatter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>In March 2014, in response to <a href="/wiki/Garda_phone_recordings_scandal" title="Garda phone recordings scandal">reports that Garda stations were bugged</a>, Kenny informed the D\xc3\xa1il that he had sent <a href="/wiki/Brian_Purcell" title="Brian Purcell">Brian Purcell</a>, the Secretary General of the Department of Justice, to <a href="/wiki/Garda_Commissioner" title="Garda Commissioner">Garda Commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Callinan" title="Martin Callinan">Martin Callinan</a>, the day before Callinan\'s sudden departure from his role. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Irish_Leaders_of_the_Opposition" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Irish Leaders of the Opposition">Leader of the Opposition</a> <a href="/wiki/Miche%C3%A1l_Martin" title="Miche\xc3\xa1l Martin">Miche\xc3\xa1l Martin</a> said this meant Kenny had effectively "sacked" Callinan. Kenny also said that he had been personally briefed on Garda surveillance by his <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Ireland" title="Attorney General of Ireland">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ire_Whelan" title="M\xc3\xa1ire Whelan">M\xc3\xa1ire Whelan</a>, as Whelan did not wish to speak of the matter over the telephone.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2014, following the resignation of Minister for Justice and Equality <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shatter" title="Alan Shatter">Alan Shatter</a>, support for Kenny and his party slumped at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Irish_local_elections" title="2014 Irish local elections">local</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_European_Parliament_election_in_Ireland" title="2014 European Parliament election in Ireland">European</a> elections.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Kenny was later to be seen doing some "happy dancing" at the annual <a href="/wiki/Bloom_Festival" title="Bloom Festival">Bloom Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In March 2015, Kenny was criticised for his lack of understanding towards <a href="/wiki/Wexford_(D%C3%A1il_constituency)" title="Wexford (D\xc3\xa1il constituency)">Wexford</a> <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TD</a> <a href="/wiki/Mick_Wallace" title="Mick Wallace">Mick Wallace</a>\'s inability to speak <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, during leader\'s questions in the D\xc3\xa1il.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2015, Kenny told the D\xc3\xa1il a tale about a man with two pints in one hand. <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_Sinn_F%C3%A9in" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Leader of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a> <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams" title="Gerry Adams">Gerry Adams</a> immediately quizzed him on this, saying: "Two pints in one hand?".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 September 2015, Kenny controversially delayed leaders\' questions in the
