D\xc3\xa1il so that he could open the <a href="/wiki/Denis_O%27Brien" title="Denis O&#39;Brien">Denis O\'Brien</a>-controlled <a href="/wiki/Independent_News_%26_Media" title="Independent News &amp; Media">Independent News &amp; Media</a>\'s new digital hub.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Kenny had previously launched a book for <a href="/wiki/James_Morrissey" title="James Morrissey">James Morrissey</a>, the long-term paid spokesperson for O\'Brien.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A "punching gesture" made by Kenny as <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_McDonald" title="Mary Lou McDonald">Mary Lou McDonald</a> was speaking during a D\xc3\xa1il debate on the Budget on 13 October 2015, attracted public notice. McDonald later responded by saying, "a punching gesture is unusual behaviour to say the least and I would suggest not to be repeated".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later that month, Kenny told a gathering of the <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People&#39;s Party">European People\'s Party</a> (EPP) in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, that he had been instructed to have the army guarded ATMs, during the economic downturn. Opposition TDs wondered why he did not tell this to the banking inquiry and Kenny was accused of "telling a tall tale". Kenny himself later contradicted his own account by saying he had not received a specific briefing on the matter. A spokesman for Kenny later claimed it had been "informally discussed" in <a href="/wiki/Government_Buildings" title="Government Buildings">Government Buildings</a> in early 2012, but that minutes had not been kept due to the sensitivity of the details therein.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 3 February 2016, Kenny announced his intention to request that <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Higgins</a> dissolve the <a href="/wiki/31st_D%C3%A1il" class="mw-redirect" title="31st D\xc3\xa1il">31st D\xc3\xa1il</a>. He told the D\xc3\xa1il before its dissolution that the <a href="/wiki/2016_Irish_general_election" title="2016 Irish general election">2016 general election</a> would occur on Friday, 26 February.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At a Fine Gael rally in his home town of Castlebar, County Mayo, on 20 February 2016, Kenny informed an audience that his local constituents were All-Ireland champion "whingers". He later told media in <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>, that he was referring to local Fianna F\xc3\xa1il members.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the election, Fine Gael received <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_32nd_D%C3%A1il" title="Members of the 32nd D\xc3\xa1il">50 seats</a>, 29 short of an overall majority. <a href="/wiki/2016_Irish_government_formation" title="2016 Irish government formation">Preliminary discussions</a> took place with <a href="/wiki/List_of_Irish_Leaders_of_the_Opposition" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Irish Leaders of the Opposition">Leader of the Opposition</a> <a href="/wiki/M%C3%ADche%C3%A1l_Martin" class="mw-redirect" title="M\xc3\xadche\xc3\xa1l Martin">M\xc3\xadche\xc3\xa1l Martin</a>, in order to agree on an arrangement to support either Kenny, Fine Gael or under a new leader to <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_32nd_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 32nd D\xc3\xa1il">remain in government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 10 March 2016, Kenny resigned as Taoiseach, after failing to win enough votes to be elected for a second term. He and the cabinet continued in a caretaker capacity until a new government was formed.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As caretaker Kenny went to <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, as usual for Saint Patrick\'s Day. There he was reported as having told the Irish Embassy: "Bejaysus, I wish I didn\'t have to go back and face what I have to face".<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> He also met President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, as part of the annual visit of the Taoiseach to the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>, for the handing over of the bowl of <a href="/wiki/Shamrock" title="Shamrock">shamrock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 April 2016, an agreement was reached with Fianna F\xc3\xa1il to allow a Fine Gael-led minority government, and on 6 May 2016, Kenny was elected Taoiseach again, by a margin of 59 to 49 votes (with 51 abstentions), and formed a <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_32nd_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 32nd D\xc3\xa1il">government</a>. He became the first member of Fine Gael to win re-election as Taoiseach in Ireland\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-Reelection_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reelection-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Kenny also took over as <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Defence_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Defence (Ireland)">Minister for Defence</a>, from Simon Coveney, who became the new <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Housing,_Planning_and_Local_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for Housing, Planning and Local Government">Minister for Housing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Regarding the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">United Kingdom European Union membership referendum</a>, Kenny went on record as saying the possibility of a "<a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>" would cause a "serious difficulty" with maintaining peace in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> He was described as favouring Britain remaining in the European Union, for were Britain to leave the EU, the peace settlement in Northern Ireland might collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> This statement was denounced by <a href="/wiki/Theresa_Villiers" title="Theresa Villiers">Theresa Villiers</a>, the British <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Northern_Ireland" title="Secretary of State for Northern Ireland">Secretary of State for Northern Ireland</a>, as "scaremongering of the worst possible kind"; she stated that the <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a>, the "open border" encompassing the United Kingdom and Ireland, would not be affected by Britain\'s departure from the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_(34005795892).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg/220px-Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg/330px-Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg/440px-Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_%2834005795892%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photo_of_the_Day_3_17_17_(34005795892).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kenny with US President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, 16 March 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>On 30 January 2017, a joint press meeting was held between Enda Kenny and <a href="/wiki/British_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="British Prime Minister">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Merrion_Street" title="Merrion Street">Merrion Street</a>, Dublin, to discuss the implications of Brexit on Northern Ireland and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Subsequent to the <a href="/wiki/2016_Irish_general_election" title="2016 Irish general election">2016 general election</a>, there were calls for him to step down as Leader of Fine Gael, and thus as Taoiseach. After the uncovering of the Garda smear campaign of sergeant <a href="/wiki/Maurice_McCabe" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurice McCabe">Maurice McCabe</a>, some backbench TDs lost confidence in Kenny.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Kenny had stated he would indicate his plans for a leadership change following his return from the US for the traditional St. Patrick\'s Day celebrations; however, at the St. Patrick\'s Day parade in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, Kenny stated that he would not stand down from leadership until the issues of Brexit and the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2017_Northern_Ireland_Assembly_election" title="2017 Northern Ireland Assembly election">snap election in Northern Ireland</a> had been resolved, saying that "you can\'t have a situation where you have no leadership in Northern Ireland and where we have to define from a European Union point of view where Ireland would be, what the agreed terms of reference for the [Brexit] negotiations are". He also remarked that he and Prime Minister May were in agreement that there would not be a return to direct rule from Westminster in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> On 20 March, Finance Minister Michael Noonan stated that Kenny should remain in office at least until June, when the next phase of EU Brexit negotiations was set to begin. The following day, Kenny announced that he would not consider standing down until May at the earliest, and that he planned to attend the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> on 29 April 2017, to discuss strategy surrounding Brexit.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 17 May 2017, Kenny announced his intention to step down as party leader, effective at midnight.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> He requested that the party conclude the election of his <a href="/wiki/2017_Fine_Gael_leadership_election" title="2017 Fine Gael leadership election">successor</a> by 2 June 2017, and said that he would step down as Taoiseach shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-Resignation_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resignation-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In the ensuing election, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Social_Protection" title="Minister for Social Protection">Minister for Social Protection</a> <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a> was elected Leader of Fine Gael.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In a statement, Kenny offered his "heartiest congratulations" to Varadkar, saying "this is a tremendous honour for him and I know he will devote his life to improving the lives of people across our country".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early June 2017, Kenny made his final trip to the U.S. as Taoiseach. While in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> on 4 June 2017, he was in attendance at <a href="/wiki/Soldier_Field" title="Soldier Field">Soldier Field</a> for Irish rock band <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>\'s performance as part of their <a href="/wiki/The_Joshua_Tree_Tour_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="The Joshua Tree Tour 2017">Joshua Tree Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> U2 lead singer <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a> dedicated their performance of the song "<a href="/wiki/Trip_Through_Your_Wires" title="Trip Through Your Wires">Trip Through Your Wires</a>" to Kenny,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> saying "The man we call Taoiseach, which I think might mean head of the house or something like that... The chieftain of our country is here tonight! ...We\xe2\x80\x99d like to honour our graceful leader."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 June 2017, Kenny tendered his resignation as Taoiseach. The following day, 14 June 2017, he nominated Varadkar to formally succeed him as Taoiseach in the D\xc3\xa1il; the D\xc3\xa1il approved the nomination. Kenny then made his farewell address to the D\xc3\xa1il, quoting U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>: "Far and away, the best prize that life has to offer is a chance to work hard at work worth doing." After receiving a standing ovation from the D\xc3\xa1il, Kenny departed for <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ras_an_Uachtar%C3%A1in" title="\xc3\x81ras an Uachtar\xc3\xa1in">\xc3\x81ras an Uachtar\xc3\xa1in</a> and submitted his resignation to President <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a>. In his last duty as Taoiseach he advised the President that the D\xc3\xa1il had nominated Varadkar as Taoiseach, and that the President should thus invite him to form a new government and appoint him as Taoiseach in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">constitution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Farewell_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farewell-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He is presenting an Irish language television series about old Irish railway routes on <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_One" title="RT\xc3\x89 One">RT\xc3\x89 One</a> in 2021, called <i>Iarnr\xc3\xb3d Enda</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>It commenced broadcasting on Easter Monday 5 April 2021 at 8:30 p.m finishing up on Monday 10 May after 6 weeks.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-political_activity">Post-political activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Post-political activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Return_to_the_backbenches_.282017.E2.80.932020.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_the_backbenches_(2017\xe2\x80\x932020)">Return to the backbenches (2017\xe2\x80\x932020)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Return to the backbenches (2017\xe2\x80\x932020)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 29 December 2017, Kenny was a wedding guest of Fine Gael <a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Buttimer" title="Jerry Buttimer">Jerry Buttimer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>. When a reporter took the opportunity to remind him of a nearby event centre of which Kenny had "<a href="/wiki/Groundbreaking" title="Groundbreaking">turned the sod</a>" nearly two years previously, but of which the construction was now halted, Kenny made it known he was there to attend a marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2018, Kenny was named \'Irish European of the Year\' for "his outstanding contribution to promoting and developing Ireland\'s place in Europe through some of the most challenging circumstances in our history around the time of the Brexit referendum to also chairing the European Council and developing and promoting our relationship with the European Union".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2019, <i>RT\xc3\x89 Investigates</i> reported that Kenny had voted in the D\xc3\xa1il on just three occasions in 2019 (two of those votes taking place on the same day), and had missed 96% of votes that took place between June 2017 and July 2019. In total, he had voted just 15 times in that period out of a possible 400 votes. The report stated that Kenny\'s attendance in the D\xc3\xa1il had been registered on 263 days during that period, and that he had claimed the full travel and accommodation allowance of \xe2\x82\xac47,000 to which he was entitled, in addition to his salary.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Kenny\'s tenure as Taoiseach was dominated by the introduction of austerity policies in the aftermath of the economic recession.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> These policies began under the previous Fianna F\xc3\xa1il government in 2008, and continued for much of his first term. Overall, the impact of these budgets has been described as not conforming to "either a progressive pattern (losses increasing with income) or regressive pattern (losses declining with income)" by the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Social_Research_Institute" title="Economic and Social Research Institute">Economic and Social Research Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political journalist John Downing wrote a biography of Kenny titled <i>Enda Kenny: The Unlikely Taoiseach</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Kenny has been married to <a href="/wiki/Fionnuala_Kenny" title="Fionnuala Kenny">Fionnuala O\'Kelly</a> since 1992. She has been described by the media as his "secret weapon".<sup id="cite_ref-endas_secret_weapon_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endas_secret_weapon-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> O\'Kelly is a first cousin to sitting Fine Gael <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a> <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Kelly_(Irish_politician)" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Kelly (Irish politician)">Se\xc3\xa1n Kelly</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> who also served as a President of the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> (GAA). The O\'Kelly family originally come from the parish of Kilcummin near <a href="/wiki/Killarney" title="Killarney">Killarney</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Kerry" title="County Kerry">County Kerry</a>. The couple have three children: one daughter, Aoibhinn, and two sons, Ferdia and Naoise. The couple met in <a href="/wiki/Leinster_House" title="Leinster House">Leinster House</a>, where O\'Kelly worked as a press officer for Fianna F\xc3\xa1il. She later worked with <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann">Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann</a> (RT\xc3\x89).<sup id="cite_ref-endas_partys_best_asset_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endas_partys_best_asset-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-endas_secret_weapon_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endas_secret_weapon-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kenny has climbed <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a> and completed the <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Kerry" title="Ring of Kerry">Ring of Kerry</a> Charity Cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> He is a keen supporter of his native <a href="/wiki/Mayo_GAA" title="Mayo GAA">Mayo GAA</a> football team, and played <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">football</a> for his local club, <a href="/wiki/Islandeady_GAA" title="Islandeady GAA">Islandeady GAA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> of which he is the current club president. His father Henry, won an <a href="/wiki/All-Ireland_Senior_Football_Championship" title="All-Ireland Senior Football Championship">All-Ireland</a> medal with the county team in 1936. His grandfather was a <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse_keeper" title="Lighthouse keeper">lighthouse keeper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enda_Kenny&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style Retrieved <span class="nowrap">21 April</span> 2017</span>. <q>Mr Kenny has since apologized unreservedly and has insisted it was not intended as a racist remark. A number of those who were present accept that Mr Kenny was not setting out to be racist. "The laugh wasn\'t supposed to be provoked by the word \'nigger\'," says one Fine Gael figure. "The laugh was supposed to come from the picture of these three white guys in a bar in Portugal laughing at a Moroccan guy who dismissed a famous African leader as a \'nigger\', an epithet none of the white guys would dream of using." This is very likely to be true, but perhaps too subtle as a political justification for Mr Kenny\'s use of the word. No party source contacted yesterday would defend Mr Kenny\'s action.
